## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics) — thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: The variables indicate a constitutive relation where stress (sigma) depends on strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), typical of thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent plasticity/strain-hardening models used for metals/polymers/ceramics under quasi-static loading.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke’s law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermoelastic modulus approximation)
- Polynomial elastic nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (small-strain nonlinear elasticity with thermal dependence)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (empirical temperature-softening/stiffening of elastic response)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon/Ludwik-type, no offset): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic/flow curve with temperature-dependent strength scale)
- Linear temperature softening of strength scale: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (flow stress with temperature-dependent prefactor)
- Thermoelastic with effective mechanical strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (thermal expansion as a stress-free strain shift)
- Thermoelastic with temperature-dependent modulus and thermal strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * T) (common linearized thermoelastic form)
- Ramberg–Osgood-style inversion surrogate: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) * exp(c2 * T) (captures initial linear region then rapid hardening; used as an explicit sigma(epsilon,T) proxy)
- Saturating hardening (Voce-type in strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (yield/offset plus saturation hardening with temperature dependence)
- Combined linear+Voce hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) + (c5 + c6 * T) * epsilon (mix of saturation and linear hardening)
- Thermally activated softening in log-form (empirical): log(sigma + c0) = c1 + c2 * log(epsilon + c3) + c4 * T (often fits wide ranges while keeping sigma positive)
- Hyperelastic-inspired uniaxial surrogate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (exp(c2 * epsilon) - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (captures tension–compression asymmetry in a smooth form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon at small epsilon suggests sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon with E decreasing or increasing with T depending on material class.
- Thermal expansion as stress-free strain: appearance of (epsilon - c*T) indicates temperature-induced strain offset (thermoelastic shift) rather than pure softening.
- Temperature softening of strength: multiplicative exp(c*T) or linear (c0 + c1*T) factors on stress scale often represent decreasing flow stress with increasing T (choose sign via fitted c).
- Strain hardening behavior: power-law in epsilon (epsilon**c) implies scale-free hardening; exponential-in-epsilon terms imply rapid early hardening.
- Hardening saturation: (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) structure encodes approach to an asymptotic stress, typical of Voce-type saturation.
- Yield/offset presence: additive baseline (c0 + c1*T) suggests a yield/initial flow stress component distinct from hardening contribution.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: terms like T*epsilon or exp(c*T)*epsilon**c indicate that temperature changes both the initial slope and the curvature (hardening rate).
- Ensuring positivity of stress: modeling log(sigma + c0) or using exp(·) forms helps enforce sigma > 0 when fitting broad ranges.
- T-dependent curvature: allowing coefficients of epsilon**2 or exp(c*epsilon) to vary with T captures that temperature can change not just strength but the hardening mechanism (e.g., dynamic recovery).

Structure desc      : Affine-in-epsilon model where epsilon multiplies a sum of a constant slope, a T-dependent slope, and a cosine modulation; plus an (almost zero) constant offset. T participates linearly in the term 0.1447*T*epsilon and inside cos(T + phase), while epsilon is purely linear (no |epsilon|, powers, log/exp). The intercept c1≈5e-8 is effectively zero, and the dominant behavior is epsilon*(c2 + c3*cos(T-0.318)) with c2=-39.49 and c3=7.75, while the T*epsilon term is comparatively mild unless T is very large. Approximate simplification: epsilon*(-39.49 + 7.75*cos(T-0.318) + 0.1447*T).

- It has an `epsilon*sin(T + const)` term
- No linear terms in T, no constant offset, no linear epsilon term

Also, under the domain constraint (epsilon ≥ 0), `|epsilon| = epsilon` and `|epsilon|² = epsilon²`.
